Rice Merchants Petition for Exemption from Business Tax 191

Yesterday Representatives Were Sent to Petition Various Agencies

The Rice Merchants Association, because the Municipal Finance Bureau announced the business tax rate schedule, including the grain and rice industry in the one-thousandth tax levy, already explained that rice and grain are related to the people's livelihood and that the levy of business tax on the rice industry would only increase the burden on the people. They have already listed reasons for requesting the Municipal Finance Bureau to exempt them from the tax, but have not received approval. Upon seeing a report that the Zhejiang Provincial Government had decided to exempt the grain and rice business tax, they specially cited the case to request the Party and government agencies to exempt the Shanghai rice merchant business tax. Yesterday, they nominated representatives Lu Wenshao, Zhang Nianxuan, Shi Hongxun, Lu Jingwen, Xu Jingzhi and five other gentlemen who went to the Municipal Government at 10:00 AM, where they were received by Section Chief Luo of the Second Section. The representatives explained the purpose of their visit, stating the importance of rice and grain to people's livelihood. Section Chief Luo agreed to report this to the mayor. After the representatives excused themselves, they then went to the Municipal Finance Bureau, where they were received by Secretary Chen. After leaving, they returned to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, where they were received by Commissioner Fang, who agreed to forward the reasons to the Yuan (Executive Yuan) and the Municipal Government to request exemption based on the case. The representatives then took their leave, by which time the clock had already struck twelve. The petition document is transcribed below: It is submitted that rice and grain concern the people's livelihood, requesting that the Zhejiang precedent be followed and that business tax be exempted. I note that the Shanghai business tax rate schedule has already been issued by the Municipal Finance Bureau, stating that the rice and grain industry is subject to a one-thousandth tax on business volume, and so on. Because rice and grain are closely related to the people's livelihood, we have listed reasons and requested the Municipal Finance Bureau to grant an exemption, but no reply has been received. Recently, we saw a report that Zhejiang Province has already approved an exemption for the rice and grain industry. We wish to restate our reasons and request that the precedent be temporarily exempted. We note that Shanghai is not a rice-producing region, and the daily needs of the people depend entirely on the supply from neighboring producing areas and foreign companies. The rice and grain sold in rice stores and door markets, in rice stores and factories in the producing areas, have already been taxed. Foreign rice has already paid customs duties. If the business tax of rice shops is levied again, it would be multiple taxes on one item, which obviously violates the principle of one tax per item, this being the first point. Shanghai city has a population of 2.7 million, most of whom are poor people. Just by checking the rice sales, inferior rice and foreign varieties make up the majority, which is enough to prove the number of poor people in Shanghai. The addition of business tax to rice and grain will inevitably lead to cheap sales prices, indirectly exploiting the livelihoods of the common people, this being the second point. In the past, when lijin tax had not been abolished, other industries suffered from it, but the rice and grain industry was fortunate enough to be spared. Now that the lijin tax has been abolished, a tax has been added instead, without benefiting from the abolition of lijin tax and suffering from its harm instead, this being the third point. In recent years, disasters and crop failures have been reported repeatedly, and the price of rice has been high, increasing costs and making profits difficult. Whenever the transition between seasons is approaching, the price of rice will be high and expensive, and the community will rise up to criticize it. Government offices restrict prices, and rice shops suffer from the burden of buying high and selling low. Selling rice at retail often leads to the loss of capital. Looking back on past events, there have been many places where panic occurred due to the high price of rice. Workers demand rice allowances which leads to disputes, and labor unrest occurs frequently, creating an unstable social scene, this being the fourth point. The borders of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces are adjacent to each other, and Shanghai is especially close. Since Zhejiang Province has been granted an exemption, and the situation in Shanghai is the same as in Zhejiang Province, it should be requested according to the precedent. I respectfully request that the Executive Yuan, the Ministry of Finance, the Ministry of Industry, and the Central Party Headquarters consider the importance of food for the people and approve the Shanghai Municipal Government to follow suit and exempt the rice and grain industry from business tax in order to reduce the burden on the common people. In addition to nominating representatives to petition the Municipal Government for an exemption, the timing is pressing. We earnestly request a prompt reply for guidance. With utmost urgency, we await your command. I respectfully submit this, and so on.

Cai Zengji Concurrently Serves as Head of the Business Tax Collection Office 192

The Municipal Business Tax Preparatory Office has now completed its preparatory procedures. The office will soon be closed and the Municipal Business Tax Collection Office will be established. The internal personnel have been completely decided. The director will continue to be Cai Zengji, the director of the Finance Bureau, and the deputy director will be Cen Dechang, the secretary of the Municipal Government. The position of secretary has also been appointed to Sheng Zaiwan.

Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau Sends Miao Zhongxiu and Others to Japan 193

This Morning on the Tatsuta Maru to Investigate the Silk Industry

The Shanghai Commodity Inspection Bureau of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce has determined that the grading and inspection methods for raw silk in the United States and Japan are generally in place. Starting in January next year, Japan will implement this compulsory inspection. Furthermore, in order to alleviate the recession in the silk industry, Japan has promulgated laws and various measures that are sufficient for our country to learn from. Therefore, Director Zou presented a request to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to dispatch Miao Zhongxiu, the director of the Raw Silk Inspection Office of the Bureau, along with technical officer Dr. Li Yaobang, to Japan for investigation. They are scheduled to depart this morning (July 11th) at 5:00 AM on the Tatsuta Maru for a three-week trip and return to Shanghai around the 2nd of next month. The important objectives of the investigation are: (1) The content of Japan's implementation of raw silk grading and inspection; (2) The current situation of the Japanese silk industry. In addition to Miao and Li, the accompanying people include Wang Shiqiang, the manager of the Feiyun Silk Factory, Chen Zezhong, the manager of the Changan Silk Factory, Mao Yiqun, the manager of the Longji Silk Factory, and several others.

American Women's Alliance Severely Protests the Opium Public Sales 194

The China National Anti-Narcotics Association recently received a protest letter from the American Women's Alliance in Washington, D.C., against the opium public sales in our country, requesting the association to convey this message. The translation is as follows: The American Women's Alliance is shocked and concerned about the news that your country is currently implementing opium public sales to expand the production, sale, and distribution of opium in order to increase tax revenue. Your country has always waged a clear war against narcotics, but now it has adopted a self-destructive policy, causing countless friends of China to be saddened and disappointed. The League of Nations recently published the report of the Far East Opium Investigation Team, which described on page 27 the impact of the spread of opium addiction on society and the economy: "The ability to work gradually decreases, and it is seen that the entire living force has the possibility of disappearing. Under this situation, we dare to conclude that the average opium addict has already reduced their ability to live by 50%. As for workers who smoke opium, they have to spend 40% to 70% of their wages every day to pay for smoking, and the amount left over for personal and family daily expenses is negligible." Your country's close friend, Bishop Brent, expressed his opinion at the Geneva International Opium Conference in 1924, saying, "Our greatest contribution to helping China is to lead the Chinese government to resist all temptations to establish an opium public sales agency, or to say that we do not use this evil trade to collect huge profits, others will also take it, or to think that a country that exploits human weaknesses and evils for tax revenue cannot become a dignified government. This kind of erroneous view is deeply painful." Based on the above reasons, it was resolved by this alliance to lodge a severe protest against the implementation of opium public sales by your government. We hope that your association will convey this message.

The City's Weights and Measures to be Inspected Starting Today 195

The new system of weights and measures in this city was announced to be standardized on July 1st. The Public Security and Social Affairs Bureaus have scheduled a major inspection to begin today. The details are as follows:

Inspection Area 196

The weights and measures inspection is divided into four phases. Starting today, the first phase of the inspection in the South Shanghai District will be conducted. The Weights and Measures Inspection Office of the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau will send inspectors Ren Yiwan, Tao Yongfang, Lu Yi, and Tai Hong, led by team leader Shen Zhixing. The Public Security Bureau will send four armed police officers to conduct the joint inspection. The locations will be the guild street, Old Taiping Street, and New Taiping Street under the jurisdiction of the First District Headquarters. The inspection addresses for tomorrow will be Youche Street, Maojia Lane, Wanjuma Wharf, and Jiuda Wharf. The inspectors will be Xie Ke, Gu Fangyi, Huang Yongping, and Xu Yushu, led by team leader Wei Zhiping, and four police officers from the Public Security Bureau.

Inspection Credentials 197

When inspectors go out for inspection, they all carry inspection certificates. The contents are as follows: Shanghai Municipal Weights and Measures Inspection Office Inspector's Inspection Certificate, No. Right to Given Date, Month, Year, Director, Half-Inch Photo, (1) The validity period of this certificate, (2) This certificate is kept by the Weights and Measures Inspection Office and is temporarily signed and used by the inspectors. It shall be returned upon completion of the task. (3) The validity of this certificate is limited to the holder being ordered to perform the task and shall not be used for other purposes. (4) This certificate shall not be valid if it has been altered or if the person's photo does not match.

Inspection Procedures 198

During the inspection, if anyone is found to have an order form from a weights and measures manufacturer, they will be ordered to go and pick up the replacement quickly. Those still using old instruments will be persuaded to switch to the new system. All old instruments will be stamped for modification. After the inspection, a "Shanghai Municipal 20th Year Weights and Measures Periodic Inspection Completed Certificate" will be posted on the store door. "Certificate issued by the Shanghai Municipal Weights and Measures Inspection Office, Public Security Bureau, District Number, Station Number." At the same time, the inspector will fill out an execution inspection registration form as follows: (1) Person being inspected, (2) Address, (3) Type, capacity, and quantity of new instruments, (4) Type, capacity, and quantity of old instruments, (5) Disposal method of old instruments, (6) Inspection date, (7) Remarks, (8) Inspector's signature.

A Large-Scale International Club Planned 204

Initiated by an international banking syndicate

Meeting to be held on the 17th

An international club, established at the site of the Majestic Hotel, including its luxurious ballroom, to accommodate 2,000 members, will be formally discussed at a meeting convened at the offices of the Allied Building Company on July 17th. Mr. Li Fucun, General Manager of the Zhejiang Industrial Bank, and Mr. Spike, Manager of the Allied Building Company, jointly issued seventy invitations yesterday, inviting prominent Chinese and Western figures in Shanghai and business leaders to serve as initiators. The purchase of the Majestic Hotel, after being rejected by the foreign ratepayers at the Public Concession's annual meeting on April 15th, saw the Municipal Council relinquish its right to purchase. Consequently, the international banking syndicate acquired it for 3.5 million taels, divided into seven shares. These shares are held by the Allied Building Company, Mr. Li Fucun, and Mr. Chen Guangfu, representing the Chinese banks, Sir Robert Ho Tung, Sassoon & Co., the Yangtse Finance Corporation, and the Probst, Hanbury & Co., each holding one share. The international banking syndicate, recognizing the lack of international club facilities in Shanghai, considered it a deficiency. They proposed allocating a portion of the Majestic Hotel's premises, along with all its equipment and decorations, for the use of an international club, at a cost of 1.3 million taels. The ballroom would also continue to operate as a social hub. All handover procedures have been completed. The Majestic Hotel property covers a total of 58.593 mu, with over 23.5 mu allocated to the international club. We cannot help but admire the generosity of the international banking syndicate, considering the low cost. Given such favorable circumstances, the club's thriving future is predictable. As for the repayment plan, it is proposed to issue 6% debentures worth 1.4 million taels, with Chinese and Western individuals each subscribing to half. Thus, in addition to repaying the purchase price, there will be a surplus of 200,000 taels for development. Regarding membership, Mr. Li Fucun and Mr. Spike plan to have 500 shareholder members and 1,500 ordinary members. The club will hire one Chinese and one Western secretary each to manage the various affairs of this Shanghai social center. Additionally, an experienced European will be hired to serve as the hotel's manager. Mr. Zhang Qun, the Mayor of Shanghai, will be the first president of the club, while the vice president will be selected from among reputable Westerners in Shanghai. Female groups, regardless of nationality, are welcome to join. In addition to ordinary members, there will also be honorary members. Once formally established, a declaration will be issued stating that the club is purely a social organization and is not involved in politics. Regarding the purpose of establishing the international club, it is reported that Mr. Li Fucun and Mr. Spike will provide a brief explanation at the meeting on July 17th, emphasizing the spirit of true internationalism. Therefore, anyone residing in Shanghai, regardless of nationality, is eligible to become a member. The invitations issued to solicit initiators and participants for the July 17th meeting include the following individuals: Chinese side: Yu Qiaqing, Zhang Gongquan, Li Fucun, Chen Guangfu, Hu Mengjia, Liu Hongsheng, Rong Zongjing, Shi Liangcai, Xu Xinliu, Qian Xinzhi, Ye Zhuotang, Tang Shoumin, Qin Runqing, Robert Ho Tung, Chen Bingqian, Chen Zeqing, Chen Jian'an, Song Ziliang, Huang Rongliang, Wu Yunzhai, Zhu Boquan, Li Shuxiong, Xia Xiaofang, Zhou Zongliang, Cai Zengji, Wei Jingzhou, Dong Xian Guang, Zhang Zhuping, and others. Western side: Marshall, head of Jardine, Matheson & Co.; Austin, head of Butterfield & Swire; Arnold, head of Arnhold & Co.; Bland, head of Jardine, Matheson & Co.; Leslie, head of Asiatic Petroleum Company; Baker, head of Gilman & Co.; Batzem, head of Melchers & Co.; Sassoon, head of E.D. Sassoon & Co.; Breden, General Manager of Probst, Hanbury & Co.; Maye, head of Jebsen & Co.; Hawkins, General Manager of Shanghai Power Company; Fukushima, head of Mitsui & Co.; Funatsu of the Japanese Cotton Spinners' Association; Spike, General Manager of Allied Building Company; Howard, editor of the North-China Daily News; Speelman of the International Savings Society; and lawyers Dibak and Walter, among others.

Fight Among Workers of the French Tram Company 205

Selling tickets for mother's memorial birthday

Misunderstanding over sending public contributions

Tables and chairs flew in the Hongyun Restaurant

Resulting in injuries to two people

At 10:15 last night, a violent fight broke out among workers of the French Tram Company at the Southeast Hongyun Restaurant, numbers 67-69, on the vegetable market road in the French Concession. Two people, a ticket seller and a driver, were injured on the spot. The details are recorded below.

Workers Divided into Two Factions 206

It is said that the entire workforce of the French Tram Company, located in various places, is mostly composed of local, Hubei, Shandong, and Jiangbei workers, divided into two major factions: the Liu faction, led by Liu Degong, a Shandong native and ticket inspector number 20, and the Li faction, led by Li Linshu, a Jiangbei native and inspector number 2.

Sending Public Contributions for Memorial Birthday 207

Since the entire group is divided into two factions, opinions inevitably diverge. Yesterday was the memorial birthday of the mother of Cai Hongjun, a local ticket seller number 18. Cai sent out invitations to a banquet at the Southeast Hongyun Restaurant, numbers 67-69 on Vegetable Market Road. A portion of the Shandong faction, about thirty people, initiated a collection of public contributions, with each person contributing three small silver coins to purchase a silk banner.

Light Gifts Served with Meager Dishes 208

At 10:00 last night, the guests gathered. Some of the workers from Cai's faction expressed dissatisfaction, believing that the three-coin public contribution was deliberately insulting to Cai. They immediately checked the gift registry and served a bowl of clear water and a table of the cheapest dishes to those who had participated in the three-coin public contribution and attended the banquet, as a form of retaliation. Unexpectedly, there were further twists and turns within.

Anger Transferred to the Initiators 209

It is said that some workers did not know that the public contribution was only three coins when they collected it. When they arrived at the Hongyun Restaurant and saw the host's meager treatment, they realized it contained a retaliatory motive. They then transferred their anger to some of the initiators of the public contribution. When the initiators arrived, they were attacked by the group. Tables, chairs, and miscellaneous objects were thrown down from upstairs. The two sides fought each other for a long time.

Resulting in Injuries to Two People 210

It is reported that one of the injured was driver number 164 and the other was ticket seller number 178. Upon hearing the news, the French police dispatched many detectives to suppress the situation. The streets were littered with broken chairs and benches, and onlookers blocked the road. The injured have been sent to the hospital by police car. The above situation was personally described by workers present at the scene.

Wife Sues Husband for Trafficking, Requests Divorce 211

Judge Advises Reconciliation

Plaintiff Firmly Opposes

Gao Chou, a Ningbo woman currently residing at number 84, Lower Sea Temple, has recently retained a lawyer to sue her husband for repeated trafficking and request a divorce from the Special District Court. The gist of her lawsuit is as follows: She was betrothed to the defendant, Gao Kangbao, as a child and married him at the age of seventeen. Because his family was poor, all living expenses were initially covered by pawning her dowry. However, he continued to wander and neglected his duties. Later, he had a far-fetched idea to sell the plaintiff. In March of the fifteenth year, the plaintiff came to Shanghai to work as a servant to earn a living. In December of the nineteenth year, the defendant tracked her down to Shanghai, hoping to live together. Considering that they were husband and wife, they formed a family in Mingyuan Fang on Huade Road. For a long time, they lived in harmony, but later he became acquainted with hooligans, repeatedly demanded money, and colluded with Wang A-jin, the second landlord, intending to sell her a second time. Upon learning of this, she opposed him, and he beat her. After someone intervened and persuaded him, she was spared. She was forced to request a divorce. Yesterday, Judge Zhou Daren heard the case in the civil court. The plaintiff first testified as above, stating that she was severely beaten on April 2nd of this year. She called the police, but after begging, she was not taken to the police station. After the police left, he became vicious again and threatened to sell her. She had no choice but to seek legal relief. Gao Kangbao denied the assault and trafficking, claiming that the plaintiff was having an affair with Wu Yongsheng, which is why she filed for divorce. Judge Zhou advised the plaintiff to drop the lawsuit and instructed the defendant to treat her well, so as to avoid separating after six years of marriage. However, Gao Chou was quite resolute and strongly opposed it. The debate then began and was declared closed, with a date set for sentencing.

Riverside Garden Opens in Minhang 212

Featuring Swimming Pools and Ball Courts

Shanghai-Minhang Shuttle Bus Service

Minhang Town, located southwest of Shanghai, is sixty li away. The town faces the river and borders a canal, creating a natural landscape. In the past, a local magnate, Mr. Li Yingshi, raised a large sum of money to purchase land and build the Shanghai-Minhang Highway, facilitating transportation. Trees are planted along both sides of the road, providing shade. During the summer, Chinese and Western people from Shanghai come to visit after work, constantly passing along the road or strolling along the river. However, there was no place to rest. This summer, the business community in the town opened a Riverside Garden on the southern end of the Shanghai-Minhang Road, along the Huangpu River. The garden features a ball court, swimming pool, Western-style restaurant, and small tile-roofed houses with elegant seating surrounded by bamboo fences. Under the shade of the trees, winding paths and thatched pavilions create a refreshing atmosphere. In recent days, the tourists coming are like clouds and all of them admired the scenery. The air is clean, beneficial to the body and mind. The scenery is especially good. The Shanghai-Minhang Long-Distance Bus Company opened a special shuttle bus service upon the passenger's request until 7:00 pm. Also, the garden has a lodge to accommodate guests. The riverbank has steamships for passengers to ride on, but regrettably, the supply often cannot meet the demand. Currently, a wealthy merchant has invested and surveyed the riverbank to build a world-class hotel, so that tourists from Europe and the Americas can come to experience the natural scenery of Shanghai.

Gonghexing Escapes Pirates, Runs Aground 213

The Beikou Sandboat Gonghexing recently loaded soybean oil and northern goods worth forty to fifty thousand taels from Yufeng Company in Dalian and set sail for Shanghai. However, when it sailed to the northwest of Jishan Island, it suddenly encountered a large group of pirates. Five or six pirate ships sailed onto the sea to inspect merchant ships. When they saw the Gonghexing approaching, the pirate ships surrounded it from all sides. Seeing this, the Gonghexing knew they were pirate ships and quickly set sail, but the pirate ships chased after it relentlessly and fired more than ten shots at the merchant ship. Several holes were shot in the Gonghexing's mast, and two crew members were wounded by bullets. There were more than twenty people on board the Gonghexing. Seeing two crew members injured, they tried their best to resist and simultaneously unfurled the sails and sped away. The pirate ships pursued them for two or three hours. Seeing that the Gonghexing was sailing very fast, they stopped chasing. The Gonghexing saw that the pirate ships were trailing behind them and the distance was gradually widening, and the crew's fear subsided slightly. Soon, the pirate ships disappeared, and they escaped danger. However, although the Gonghexing was not robbed by pirates, the crew was frightened and sailed in a panic. Because the sails were fully unfurled, the ship sailed too fast and ran aground on a sandbar in the middle of the Jishan sea. The bow of the ship was buried in the sandbar, causing damage. The soybean oil in the baskets was shaken and damaged, and the oil leaked out. The Gonghexing's owner, Mr. Lu, came to Shanghai from Haimen by boat to report the cargo number and hired a tugboat to tow the ship out of danger and unload the cargo to inspect the ship. It is reported that the losses suffered are already considerable.

Young Girl Cooling Off in the Dark, Neighbor Uses It as an Excuse for Extortion 215

Claims She Was Committing Adultery in Public

Demands Seventy Dollars in Compensation

Xu Fen, a girl from Taizhou, is twenty-eight years old and has a fair appearance. Previously, due to the hardship of rural life and extreme poverty at home, she came to Shanghai with a fellow villager in January of this year and stayed at the boarding house opened by Miao Jutian at number 71, Hehe Workshop, Robert Road in western Shanghai. The owner of the boarding house helped her find work in a yarn factory to make a living. Since the girl was of marriageable age and had a smart demeanor, there were many people who coveted her. At about 10:00 pm the day before yesterday, the girl was cooling off nearby. A neighbor, Wang Deyi, went out on business. After walking a few steps, he suddenly caught sight of a man and a woman committing adultery in a dark place behind the house. Wang then stepped forward to investigate. The girl Xu ran away, and the man also escaped. At that time, Wang did not make any accusations. Yesterday morning, Wang gathered more than ten burly men and, with a menacing aura, rushed to Miao's boarding house, claiming that Miao's boarding house girl, Xu Fen, was committing adultery in public last night, offending his luck and causing him to have chills and fever. Miao needed to compensate him seventy dollars and host a feast, otherwise, they would resort to force. Upon hearing this, Miao was extremely shocked. He asked the girl, who denied it and claimed it was not true. Seeing that the situation was not good, Miao called the police to the scene, who arrested Wang Deyi and four others, along with the girl and Miao You, and took them all back to the sixth district police station, accusing Wang Deyi and others of gathering a crowd to extort money. After questioning by the district chief, according to the plaintiff Miao Jutian, he was fifty-two years old, from Taizhou, and operated a boarding house at number 71, Hehe Workshop. Today, Wang Deyi suddenly came and claimed that the boarding house girl Xu Fen was committing adultery along the road, offending his luck and demanding seventy dollars in extortion and hosting a feast. According to the girl Xu Fen's confession, she was sixteen years old, from Taizhou, and was cooling off with Miao You last night. She did not have any intimate relations with anyone. According to Miao You's confession, she was forty-nine years old, and her words were the same as those of the girl. According to the defendants' confessions, one named Wang Deyi, thirty-four years old, from Taizhou, worked in a factory; one named Luo Xiaosizi, twenty-nine years old, from Qingjiang; one named Li Hailin, twenty-six years old, from Yangzhou; one named Zeng Dayuan, twenty-nine years old, from Qingjiang; and one named Bai Changhai, thirty-five years old, from Qingjiang. After obtaining the confessions, the district chief considered the case to involve gathering a crowd to extort money and prepared a document to transfer it to the General Bureau for interrogation.

Pudong Extortionist Confesses 217

Jiang Xiguang Tries His Best to Expose

Zhai Miaogen Confesses to Writing Letters

Jiang Xiguang and Zhai Miaogen, from Pudong, were arrested for repeatedly writing threatening letters between last autumn and June of this year to extort a large sum of money from Jiang Weibin, a local resident at number 16, Fengtian Road. The arrests were made by Chinese and Western detectives from the Harbin police station. Qian Zhenmiao, also a local resident, was arrested for being implicated in the case, but after questioning, the court determined that he was not involved in the case and was released on bail with the condition that he be available for questioning at any time. The charges against Jiang and Di remained. Yesterday morning, Judge Xiao Xieqian presided over a hearing in the third criminal court. The police lawyer, Li Zhishan, presented the case, stating that no other cases had been discovered during the postponement. When questioned, Jiang Xiguang firmly stated, "I am a relative and foster brother of the plaintiff and would never do such a thing. On the day of my arrest, I recognized that the handwriting on the threatening letters was Zhai's, so I had my father secretly lead the police detectives to arrest him. How could he not hate me? That is why he is incriminating me in court. His behavior is despicable. From a loan incident, it can be seen that he used someone else's name to borrow money from lenders, and therefore I broke off relations with him. If I had conspired with him in this case, I would gladly be shot. Moreover, the location agreed upon in the threatening letters was a pit latrine near the Longwang Temple in Pudong, right across from his residence, to observe the situation." When questioned, Zhai Miaogen confessed, "The facts are that Jiang Xiguang instructed me. Before, in a loan incident, he was indeed the one who borrowed money from others as collateral, but he used a small amount, so it did not suit his purpose. He came to me for money. Before this incident occurred, Jiang Xiguang came and said that the plaintiff Jiang Weibin had recently sold a house for 120,000 yuan, so he repeatedly came to me to write the threatening letters. Because Jiang knew his handwriting, he is now arrested and cannot deny it. I request the court to impose a lenient sentence because I have a blind father and a wife and children in their sixties who depend on me for support. If I am given a long-term sentence, my family will starve to death." As he spoke, tears welled up in his eyes. Jiang Xiguang, hearing this, loudly said, "His father is a well-known gangster in that area. Please, Your Honor, punish him severely." Judge Xiao verified the confessions and instructed both sides' lawyers to argue their cases before ordering that they be remanded in custody pending sentencing.

The First Sound of Zhonghe Shaole 220

Our country's music, since ancient times, has regarded Zhonghe Shaole as the highest and most valuable music, which is what Confucius called perfect and beautiful music. Its advantage is that it can withstand full research. The dynasties of all ages have respected and valued it. They promulgated its score to all provinces and counties, and selected outstanding disciples from the scholars to serve in the music and dance positions (named Yisheng, commonly known as half-head scholars), whose qualifications were equal to today's middle school graduates. The country was very grand, but the people in charge (education officials, county officials, etc.) did not know how to seek truth from facts, but instead encroached on public funds from it, so that many musical instruments were incomplete and inaccurate. At ordinary times, they did not supervise the Yisheng's practice, only rehearsing once or twice a year during the grand sacrifice. The performers didn't know what they were playing, and how could the listeners hear it. The Datong Music Society in this city has always been committed to organizing national music. The basic work must be based on Shaole as the premise. The entire orchestra members of the association have taken on the responsibility of practicing. The musical instruments used are based on the Yuan Dynasty system. (All musical instruments used in the Yuan Dynasty's worship of Confucius are collected.) Those that can be collected are also used. Coincidentally, this music is mature. It coincided with the 50th anniversary of Mr. Yu Yeqing, who was one of the committee members recommended by the association. It is appropriate to celebrate together, and the crown cover is very prosperous, which is a good opportunity for publicity. It is scheduled to be held on Saturday and Tuesday at the Italian Hall of the Majestic Hotel for the first performance. Shaole, which has been respected for thousands of years, is now suddenly revived in the world and performed publicly. The ears and eyes are refreshed. Isn't it a grand event? It is also heard that the association is also planning ancient dances, either running a primary school or contacting nearby primary schools to select 64 students and teach them various ancient dances to achieve perfection.

Wusong Ship Capsizes 221

Twenty-two passengers and crew members fall into the water with the ship

A cucumber vendor, Mr. Wang, drowns on the spot

A ship belonging to the Wusong shipping household, Gao Ayu, specializes in running between Song and Shanghai, carrying cargo. The day before yesterday, the ship loaded salted goods, dried fish, and northern and southern goods worth two or three thousand gold from Yushun, Huang Changfa, Wanchunshun, and other companies in Shanghai and set sail for Song. At about 2 pm, when it reached the Yangshupu Donggou port, an Yihua Company's Rising Sun Liner was exiting. The liner passed by the ship from behind. The ship accidentally caught the liner's small rowing boat with its masts and sails, which was difficult to pull apart for a while. Unexpectedly, the ship's helmsman panicked and released the rudder, causing the ship to capsize. The cargo was all submerged, and four crew members and eighteen passengers fell into the water with the ship. Except for twenty-one people who climbed out of the cabin and stood on the bottom of the ship, a passenger, Mr. Wang, a Yang peddler who was forty-seven years old and sold cucumbers for a living, drowned on the spot. The body has not yet been recovered. The ship has now sunk to the bottom of the sea. It is reported that the shipowner, Gao Ayu, is unwilling to go to salvage the cargo.

Norwegian Sailor Drowns in the Huangpu River 222

The Norwegian merchant ship "Rarnefjell," which specializes in transporting coal, docked at the Swire Wharf in Pudong after arriving in Shanghai this time. At 10:30 PM the night before last, a sailor on board named K. G. Olessn (44 years old, Norwegian), somehow, unnoticed, jumped into the Huangpu River and committed suicide. His body sank and disappeared without a trace. It was not until 10:00 AM yesterday that it floated to the surface at the original location. It was then recovered by a fishing boat captain named Bao Gen and taken to the ship, then transported to the Customs Water Police Station. Patrolman Sun Agui was dispatched to send it to the forensic examination center on Fielun Road for examination and subsequent burial.

Collapsed House Crushes Accountant to Death 223

Zhu Shuru's Death Was Tragic

At around 5:00 AM yesterday, two rooms of the single-story folding cloth workshop at No. 2, Lane 91, Anlan Road, Nanshi, belonging to the Guangfeng Machinery Dye Factory, collapsed due to years of disrepair and continuous heavy rain. At the time, it was late at night, and everyone was fast asleep, resulting in the factory's accountant, Zhu Shuru (29 years old, from Huizhou), being crushed to death inside. After being discovered, the incident was reported to Chang Zhenshan, the watchman at the No. 13 sentry post on nearby Linyin Road, who then reported it to Chief Wang of the Second District. Chief Wang ordered a patrol officer to investigate and first had the body extracted. He also instructed the local administrator to report to the local court for an inquest. It is reported that the deceased had an elder brother and uncle doing business in Shanghai, and the factory owner, Ni Xiqing, has instructed someone to notify them.

National Traditional Chinese Medicine Community Holds Memorial Service for Zhang Shisheng Yesterday 224

The late Mr. Zhang Shisheng of Haimen, former Standing Committee Member of the National Federation of Traditional Chinese Medicine Organizations, devoted his life to the cause of Chinese medicine for nearly thirty years. His knowledge and experience were highly respected throughout the country. Unfortunately, last winter, while attending the inaugural meeting of the Central National Medical Hall, he overworked himself and caught a cold. He passed away from illness on April 16th of this year in his hometown of Haimen. The news of his death shocked and saddened both the national medical and pharmaceutical communities. Subsequently, Mr. Zhang's former friends and leaders of Shanghai's medical and pharmaceutical organizations, Ding Zhongying and Zhang Mei'an, initiated preparations for a memorial service. Medical and pharmaceutical colleagues from various regions responded enthusiastically, expressing their condolences and requesting to join the organizers to jointly commemorate him. Therefore, the preparations were very grand. Yesterday was the day of the memorial service, and the situation was as follows:

Venue Arrangement 225

The memorial service venue was set up on the second floor of the Shanghai Municipal National Medical Association at the Yizhong Company on Zhejiang Road. Above the entrance to the main hall hung a white cloth banner that read: "Memorial Service for Mr. Zhang Shisheng, Who Devoted His Life to the Cause of Chinese Medicine." Upon entering, one could see the scrolls, elegies, and eulogies sent by medical and pharmaceutical organizations from various regions. The more than five-zhang-long aisle was lined with elegies, over five hundred couplets in total, which fluttered in the wind and were quite pleasing to the eye. In the hall, a portrait of Mr. Zhang was hung. The altar table was decorated with incense, flowers, and other items. The four walls were covered with scrolls, elegies, and wreaths, creating a very solemn atmosphere. To the right of the portrait was a plain curtain where Mr. Zhang's surviving family members stood to return greetings. From 10:00 AM to 7:00 PM, there was a constant stream of guests.

Guest Sign-In 226

The organizational representatives who attended included Xue Wenyuan and Ding Zhongying from the Shanghai Municipal National Medical Association, Zhang Mei'an from the National Medicine Trade Association, Bao Tianbai from the Shanghai Traditional Chinese Medicine Specialty School, Xu Heng from the Shanghai National Medical Society, Zhang Zanchen from the Medical Community Chunqiu Society, Yan Cangshan from the Family Medicine Advisory Society, and over two hundred people from various medical and pharmaceutical organizations outside the city. Guests who attended included Xia Yingtang, Yin Shoutian, Qin Bowei, Jiang Wenfang, Huang Baozhong, Fu Yongyan, Zhu Hegao, Chen Cunren, Bao Shisheng, Song Nianzu, Ye Shiliang, Fang Jiaobo, Xu Xiangren, Shen Tingdong, Cao Zhoubi, Yang Zhongyuan, Zhao Yaonong, and Chen Piqing, totaling over seven hundred people.

Memorial Service Proceedings 227

At 3:00 PM, after the representatives from various medical and pharmaceutical organizations in Shanghai and elsewhere and all the guests had arrived, the meeting was called to order with the ringing of a bell. Mr. Xue Wenyuan presided over the ritual, assisted by Mr. Fu Yongyan and Zhang Mei'an. After the public memorial ceremony, Zhang Mei'an, Jiang Wenfang, Fu Yongyan, Qin Bowei, Bao Tianbai, and Zhao Yaonong delivered speeches in succession, their words filled with deep sorrow. Finally, Mr. Jun Chuan, representing the family members, offered thanks in accordance with protocol.

Wuxing Electric Company Bids for Generator Set 228

The Wuxing Electric Company, in order to expand its business and meet the needs of its customers, has purchased a complete set of 1,055 horsepower diesel engine and a 1,000 kVA generator. It specifically requested quotes from various machinery firms in Shanghai. It is reported that the bidding process was held on the 8th at Yi Pin Xiang. The foreign firms that attended that day included Reiss Massey & Co., Jiansin & Co., Jardine Engineering Corporation, Carlowitz & Co., Sulzer Brothers, Arnhold, Karberg & Co., Siemens China Co., Melchers & Co., Sinchon, Jebsen & Co., Schredder, Mentor & Co., Victor & Co., Metone, and Andersen, Meyer & Co., totaling fifteen companies. The company's directors, Shen Lianfang, Li Zhichao, Li Boqin, Gu Qihan, and Li Yanshi, supervisor Shen Kuanfu, chief engineer Shen Sifang, and Xu Dongren, chairman of the technical committee of the National Private Electric Power Industry Federation, were invited to be review committee members. The bidding results showed that Jiansin, Mentor & Co., and Miye were the most promising. On the evening of the 9th, the bidding continued. Jiansin withdrew. Mentor & Co. and Miye competed fiercely. In the end, Miye won the bid because it respected the company's board of directors' conditions and did not require any guarantees, and its price was also the lowest. Siemens won the generator bid. It is reported that the prices quoted by the various foreign firms differed by more than 30,000 US dollars.

Jingwu Association Chartered Ship Trip to Putuo 229

This Month, the 18th

Purely Buddhist land in our country, combining the two scenic beauties of sea and mountain, and the supreme Pure Land of Buddhism, is Putuo. Every summer, there are many tourists, but because the voyage is circuitous and takes time, travelers often feel inconvenienced. The Jingwu Athletic Association's travel group, in view of this, has chartered the Dahua Steamboat on the 18th of this month for a special trip. It will depart at 4:00 PM and arrive at Putuo at 6:00 AM the next morning. At 4:00 PM that afternoon, it will return to Shanghai on the same ship, arriving in Shanghai at 6:00 AM on the 20th. The fee is divided into seven types, ranging from five yuan to sixteen yuan. Except for the different levels of cabins, the treatment for food and other items is the same. Because the association has found that the number of people on board during previous trips to Putuo has been too crowded, this time, in order to ensure the comfort of the travelers, the quota is limited to 400 people, and registration will be closed when the quota is full.

Wireless Telegraph Rates Reduced Yesterday 235

Based on the French Franc

International wireless telegraph rates were reduced starting yesterday. The amount of the reduction is based on the French franc. Originally, each franc was equal to one yuan in Chinese currency, but recently, the price of gold has fallen, and each franc is equal to nine jiao in Chinese currency. Therefore, after this price reduction, the telegraph fee is 90% of the original price. In the future, the rise and fall of telegraph fees will also be determined by the rise and fall of the price of gold.

Information on Solving the People's Food Problem 237

Publication of "Shanghai's People's Food Problem"

The Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs established a Grain Commission in the eighteenth year of the Republic of China, with the approval of the government, to specialize in the study of all people's food problems. As there was no special work on the study of people's food in the market, the members of the committee wrote special works on various aspects of the people's food problem, focusing on the entire people's food problem, not limited to the city of Shanghai. The bureau's food administration over the years, and the Grain Commission's suggestions and reforms regarding food, were also attached to provide a reference for food administration. The book is now published, entitled "Shanghai's People's Food Problem." It is being sold by the Commercial Press and the Civilization Bookstore both locally and in other cities. The book contains more than 300,000 words, is beautifully bound, and contains thousands of illustrations. Mayor Yuejun once commented on the book, saying, "We believe that this article is not only an aid to the study of the people's food problem in Shanghai, but also those who are concerned about the people's food problem in China should have a copy in hand." This shows the content of the book.

End of the Two Railway Union Consolidation Committee 238

The Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Union Consolidation Committee, since August of the eighteenth year of the Republic of China, was appointed by the Central People's Training Committee to be composed of Lu Mingzhi, Wang Yijian, Jiang Ziqi, Zou Zhengjian, Peng Xuesheng, etc. as consolidation committee members. The consolidation committee has been established for four years since its establishment. During this period, it has been reorganized several times, and its work has been relatively smooth. The committee has successively guided the establishment of the Shanghai-Hangzhou section and the Shanghai Wusong and other machine factories unions, the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou section transportation unions, the Shanghai North Station, McGreggor Road Station, Suzhou Station, Zhenjiang, Zhenjiang Riverside Station, Ningbo train station cargo handling unions, the Yongshao section union, the Beijing-Hangzhou section tea and refreshments unions, the catering union, and other fifteen locations. Recently, the Central Party Headquarters believes that the committee's mission of consolidation has been completed and that there is no need for it to continue to exist. It has specially issued an order to the two railway special party headquarters, ordering the committee to immediately end its work and transfer it to the training department of the two railway party headquarters for reception. After receiving the order, the committee rushed to handle the handover and was dissolved yesterday (the 10th). The staff was issued one month's severance pay and sent back to their hometowns. Yesterday, all the committee members and staff were convened for a group photo as a memento. The committee members Li Dasan, Zou Zhengjian, Song Chuanji, Chen Bohua, Xu Duren, Wang Weixia, Feng Qishu, Li Bowen, Yang Hongshu, and staff members Liu Xiong, Liu Junming, Min Luo Chao, Qin Yan, Qian Baoqi, Bi Huizhu, Huang Guoying, Han Dejun, Ma Weixiao, etc. attended. After the photo, they went to the Da Zhonghua Restaurant for a banquet to connect with each other and bid farewell.

Removal and Repositioning of Two Sunken Vessels 240

The sunken vessel "Fuhai," located in the Yangtze River at 55 degrees north of the main pole of the nine-section beacon in the South Port of the Yangtze River Estuary, at a distance of 1.26 nautical miles, i.e., approximately 121 degrees 44 minutes east longitude and 31 degrees 16 minutes north latitude, has now been removed due to obstructing the navigation of Yangtze River vessels. The Maritime Survey Bureau has announced to all Yangtze River vessels that the section is now passable. In addition, the "New Daming," which was sunk by a Japanese vessel, was originally between Lianchengzhou and Zhenjiang. Now it has changed its position. The Maritime Survey Bureau has announced that the sunken vessel is now located at 280.5 degrees north of the Muyu Sand Lighthouse, at a distance of 4.2 nautical miles, i.e., 119 degrees 53 minutes east longitude and 32 degrees 12 minutes north latitude.

New Plan for the Paris Grand Theater 248

Since the Paris Grand Theater on Avenue Joffre switched to showing sound films, its business has been very prosperous. The first silent film that has been scheduled is the social cautionary film "Human Desires Overflow," which has caused a sensation throughout Europe and won a first-class medal from the German Ministry of Education. Correspondence 254

To whom it may concern:

Having read in today's edition of your esteemed newspaper the article regarding the resolution of the strike by employees of the French Municipal Council, which stated, "Wang Zhuangyong, Liu Zhigang, Tao Qipeng, and others served as negotiating committee members, and after lengthy discussions, both parties agreed and signed a resolution," I humbly believe that Mr. Tao Qipeng and I were elected as members of the Executive Committee, and we are aware of our limited abilities and heavy responsibilities and fear of failure. However, due to the public interest, we must strive to fulfill our duties. As for the negotiating representatives this time, they were Liu Zhigang, Gao Pengcheng, Qiu Gaogang, Yang Wugang, Peng Quanfu, Wang Yaogen, Pan Wenqing, Sun Shanhai, and eight others. Mr. Tao and I not only did not represent them in signing the agreement but also did not attend the negotiations at the Du residence. I am deeply concerned that this may cause misunderstandings among the employees of our association, so I am writing to request an immediate correction. Respectfully submitted to the editor of the Shenbao.

Wang Zhuangyong, Preparatory Office of the Chinese United Association of the French Concession. July 10th.

Esteemed Mr. Editor:

I am writing to you regarding the news item in the local news section of your July 5th edition concerning a divorce case involving a barren woman, and the statement that she received some form of compensation. This does not correspond with the facts. Since the beginning of this matter, your esteemed newspaper has shown care and provided detailed coverage, for which I am extremely grateful. However, based on the insistence of both parties' parents, I hired a lawyer to draw up an agreement for a divorce without any compensation whatsoever. I respectfully request a correction. With best wishes.

Respectfully,

Lü Liansheng, No. 2, Penglai Road, Shanghai. July 9th.

Special Item

Abstract Translation of the Sixth Compilation of the Feitang Report 255

(II)

Chapter Two 256

This chapter describes the origins of the extraterritorial roads, the process of their extension, and how the Municipal Council gradually developed a partial administrative management system for the extraterritorial roads and the houses accessing them. Tracing its outline, the report indicates that the development of the extraterritorial roads began as early as 1862 and 1863. At that time, as the Taiping Rebellion was nearing its end, the public concessions were crowded with refugees, and the foreign community believed that there was a need to expand the land west of the concessions to provide recreational areas. The new racecourse, located outside the western boundary, was opened in 1862. The carriage road starting from the Mud City Creek and ending at Jing'an Temple, which soon became known as Jing'an Temple Road, was also opened in the same year. This carriage road was originally operated by a private entity, and only those who had contributed funds and paid tolls could use it. However, the committee found that the income was insufficient for various purposes, so at the taxpayers' annual meeting in April 1866, a motion was passed authorizing the next Board of Directors of the Municipal Council to take over the management of Wusong Road, Jing'an Temple Road, and the surrounding roads, which Mr. Keswick, the then-Chairman of the Municipal Council, referred to as the "lungs of Shanghai." After the passage of this motion, the Municipal Council took over Jing'an Temple Road and Xujiahui Road (now Haig Road). To understand the state of the villages outside the boundaries of the public concessions in the past, one only needs to observe the current state of the places where the Municipal Council's roads near Shanghai ended. Although there was development on the suburban land adjacent to both sides of these roads, the extent of the development was very short, except for one or two miles. Generally speaking, the villages outside the boundary in the past had no roads to speak of; the creeks and country paths were the means of transportation. Therefore, foreigners inside and outside the boundary believed that their movement would be greatly restricted if roads were not built to connect to the nearby suburbs. Between 1853 and 1863, several roads were hastily designed and built for military needs to connect outside of the concessions. It is said that these military roads were built by General Gordon, including Xujiahui Road "Haig Road," the section of Xinzha Road west of Xizang Road to Jing'an Temple Road, Maigen Road, and a road leading to Zhaojiaodu. After the end of military operations, how to maintain these roads in the future became an important issue. The Chinese authorities were not prepared to take any action, but the foreigners in the concessions paid attention to this issue and tried to urge the Municipal Council to assume this maintenance responsibility. In 1869, the Municipal Council proposed to the Daotai (local governor) the conditions under which the Council would assume responsibility for maintaining certain roads, including three points: (1) the land through which the roads passed should be exempt from land tax; (2) the Daotai should provide financial assistance for road repairs; and (3) a guarantee should be given that the Daotai would adopt "effective and resolute measures to prevent the Chinese from destroying public property." The 1868 Municipal Council Annual Report contained a report from the Works Committee stating that the Municipal Council had been notified that the Daotai had consulted with Sir Alcock and agreed to donate 1,200 yuan annually to cover the maintenance costs of roads outside the concession. This amount was considered insufficient at the time, and in fact, it seems that no funds were ever donated. The issue of road tax was related to the issue of maintaining the road so that it would not be damaged, as can be seen in the report of Mr. Medhurst, the British Consul in 1871. The report mentioned the fact that local owners of land used for road construction would often cut the road surface and destroy bridges in retaliation because they had to bear the obligation of paying land tax on the land. The issue of paying land tax on land used for road construction inside and outside the public concessions was often the subject of negotiations between the Municipal Council and the Chinese authorities. This issue was resolved in 1885. (To be continued)

World Snippets 257

— Haike

Ants Heal Wounds

Ants are tiny insects in the insect world. How could they heal wounds? However, in Peru, South America, this is indeed the case. Recently, a British tourist group went to visit. It is said that they personally witnessed local doctors using ants to treat external injuries because there is a kind of ant in Peru that has a unique and powerful jaw. As long as they are placed where they can bite, they will immediately open their mouths and bite firmly, not letting go. Therefore, if the natives suffer any injuries to their skin, they seek treatment from a doctor. The doctor will squeeze the wound tightly together and pick up an ant from the ground and place it on the wound, with its head touching the injured area. It will immediately bite with its large jaws, sewing the wound together. Then, the doctor will cut off the ant's body and place other ants on the wound, one by one, in the same way, until the entire wound is completely sewn up. Such a treatment method is truly unheard of.

Crocodile Reward

In the Berlin Zoo in Germany, a thousand crocodiles were once transported from America, ready for display. The director of the zoo, in order to make the public aware, used a large balloon to fly over the zoo grounds, attracting the attention of the audience. The balloon had large words written on it: "One Thousand Crocodiles." However, the weight of the balloon was too heavy, and the anchor tying it down was relatively light. Before long, the balloon soared into the sky, reaching over nine thousand feet, and gradually disappeared. Therefore, the director of the zoo took advantage of this opportunity to publicize the event widely, saying that anyone who found the balloon and returned it to the zoo would be rewarded with a live crocodile, a promise that would not be broken.

Interesting Anecdotes of the Same Names in Ancient and Modern Times 258

— Jiaolou

It is often the case that there are people with the same names in ancient and modern times. Since Emperor Yuan of Liang had a book called "A Record of People with the Same Names in Ancient and Modern Times," many people have continued to write such records. Recent names, such as Xu Shichang, Jiang Chaozong, Zhang Hu, Ma Liang, and Wang Zhen, all existed in ancient times. There is also a Shanghai police officer named Zhang Liang, who also belongs to this category. Now, I will take a few cases of people with the same names recorded in the Shanghai news of this newspaper in recent years and offer some other interpretations for amusement. The dates of publication have mostly been forgotten, but I think readers should still have them in mind.

Su Xun Posts an Advertisement to Find a Husband for His Daughter

Note: Su Xun is Su Laoquan of the Song Dynasty. His daughter, Su Xiaomei, was proud of her talent and was very picky in choosing a spouse. The novel's description of the three difficulties for the groom can summarize it. It is fitting that his advertisement to find a husband must be in the form of a public announcement.

Meng Haoran Causes Trouble While Drinking

Note: Li Bai's poem to Meng Haoran says, "Often intoxicated by the moon, he does not serve the ruler because of flowers." It is known that Haoran liked to drink. But he did not have the style of Guan Fu scolding people while sitting, so why would he cause trouble? This is why he is the Meng Haoran of Zhabei. (The newspaper reported that the person lived in Zhabei)

Zhao Ziang Falls from a Horse

Note: Zhao Ziang is Zhao Mengfu. He was famous at the time for his skill in painting horses. Even today, obtaining an inch of his painting is hailed as a precious treasure. How could he be known for falling from a horse? Perhaps the son of a good doctor must die from medicine, and the son of a good shaman must die from ghosts. Someone who is good at painting horses must suffer from horses. Just a laugh.

Song Yu is Smeared

Note: Song Yu was a handsome man from Chu. There was a girl next door who spied on him for three years. It is to be expected that Song Yu would be smeared. The new criminal law also has a clause for women raping men. But the current Song Yu is not male but female. If she marries the Song Yu of Chu, they would truly be a perfect match.

The Capital After the Heavy Rain 259

— Wang Xingyuan

For the past ten days, the weather has been hot and humid, making people feel stifled. Although it is already summer, the climate is so sultry that we have long anticipated that heavy rain would fall soon. Then, on the evening of the third day, dark clouds filled the sky, thunder roared, and torrential rain poured down continuously. Everywhere was a sea of white water, almost turning into a swamp. It has truly been a rare sight in more than ten years. I will record what I have seen and heard and tell the readers.

Water Accumulates on Zhongshan Road

The most prominent road in the capital is the newly built Zhongshan Road, which is flat and wide, almost comparable to Nanjing Road in Shanghai. After the heavy rain, the water had not yet been drained, and it accumulated to a foot deep. The lower places are even worse. Pedestrians had to lift their clothes to pass, with the water almost reaching their knees. Cars sped back and forth, splashing water, truly a spectacular sight.

Rickshaw Pullers Profit Threefold

The water had risen greatly, and pedestrians had a great sigh of helplessness. As a result, rickshaws were all booked up, and prices rose by two or three times. The rickshaw pullers were overjoyed, but running wildly in the rain, their clothes soaked, was also a hardship.

Fashionable Young Ladies in a Dilemma

When the reporter went from Xiaguan to Xinjiekou for business, the rain was still light. Passing through Gulou, there were two young ladies wearing silk stockings and leather shoes, dressed beautifully, walking on the road. Suddenly, torrential rain poured down, and they could not avoid it. Their bodies were completely drenched, like chickens that had fallen into the water. It was laughable and also pitiful.

The Water in the Qinhuai River Almost Reached the Banks

After this heavy rain, the water in the Qinhuai River also rose several feet, almost reaching the banks. If there is no sign of clear weather, the houses on both sides will all be in the water.

People from Jiangbei Cry Out in Misery

People from Jiangbei gathered in the Xiaguan area, living in sheds. The ground was all low-lying. After the rain, the water rose, and many sheds collapsed. Those that did not collapse were all immersed in water, making it difficult to find a place to settle down. Everyone had a sad look on their faces, and their condition was extremely pitiful.

The River Water Rose Violently and Vastly

Since the beginning of summer, the water level in the Yangtze River has risen remarkably. After this heavy rain, the river water rose even more than ten feet, vast and surging, almost reaching the banks. In addition, the violent wind blew and stirred up angry waves, which were irresistible. It was also a spectacular sight.

Talking About the Nail Decoration of Parisian Women 260

— Yanyu

Paris is the most prosperous city in the world, which has long been famous. Its pursuit of extravagance in makeup is unparalleled. Even London and New York cannot compare. Recently, women in that country have been competing to decorate their nails as an elegant activity in their boudoirs, fighting each other for innovation, and it has become a popular trend. I will excerpt a few examples to share with readers.

Identifying Women by Their Nails

In today's French society, if we want to identify whether a woman is fashionable or not, we only need to examine the nails of her slender fingers to see if they have undergone exquisite decoration. Nowadays, almost all French women who slightly frequent social occasions no longer want to retain the natural beauty of their nails without adding color or drawing patterns.

Nails and Dresses in the Same Color

If we stroll through the streets of Paris, we can immediately see that the color of the nail polish on women's nails is often the same as the color of their dresses. At present, the most popular women's clothing material in Paris is light blue, so the nails of those women are mostly dyed light blue to match. This method of dyeing nails is very simple, like using rouge for cheeks or lipstick for lips. However, before dyeing, a layer of colloidal water needs to be applied to prevent fading. However, it can also be wiped off at any time, so the nail polish of fashionable women often changes several times a day depending on their dresses.

Spending a Fortune on Painting Nails

Parisian dancer Meiboli earns more than ten times more per month than the French president, and her extravagant lifestyle is comparable to that of a queen or concubine. Her clothing and makeup are always imitated by fashionable women all over the country. Whenever Meiboli has a new outfit, it will become popular on the market in a few days. Since the trend of nail decoration became popular, ladies have come up with new styles one after another and have made many contributions. Recently, she specially hired the famous French painter Stederborg to paint exquisite and delicate colorful flowers and birds on each nail. From then on, the snow-white skin and slender fingers are even more beautiful with the famous paintings, making them even more charming. It is said that the cost of painting the nails is no less than a thousand US dollars.

Free Talk Editorial Department

Random Thoughts on Traveling in Korea (2) 262

— Jiping

Regarding the anti-Chinese riot in Korea, according to Mr. Hayashi, the representative of the Japanese Chargé d'Affaires, Mr. Shigemitsu, when he visited the Korean Foreign Minister, it has returned to stability. However, bad news has come that our country's Consulate General was destroyed by rioters on the night of the 8th. Not a single piece of equipment or document survived. Consulate staff have temporarily taken refuge in the Governor-General's Office. Among the 3,000 Chinese expatriates seeking refuge in the consulate, many have been killed or injured, a truly tragic sight. The Korean authorities have neither protected foreign nationals nor even provided safe protection for the diplomatic representatives of friendly nations. The so-called "nearby, one does not hear the sound of thunder; staring, one does not see the shape of Mount Tai" is a truly bizarre failure of responsibility. In today's world with might but without justice, to whom can we appeal? But we must uphold justice and declare the truth to the world.

Speaking of the Korean Consulate General, I am filled with anger. I remember when I was in Seoul, I went there every day to visit friends. Upon entering the gate, there was a Chinese expatriate elementary school. The interior of the consulate had high-rise buildings that were twice as spacious as the Japanese Embassy in Tokyo. The gardens were full of fragrant grass and beautiful flowers, and the trees were lush, with very beautiful scenery. Recalling that when Yuan Shikai was the Commercial Commissioner, the flat buildings behind the consulate were all the barracks for his guards. When he went out, he was surrounded by guards in front and behind, with great pomp and circumstance. There were Chinese police in the city, and Chinese training grounds outside the city. The right to govern was in our hands, and the Koreans sang praises. Later, after the defeat in the Sino-Japanese War, Korea was annexed by Japan, and all special rights were completely revoked. Looking at those flat buildings now, leaning and dilapidated, the sight is full of sadness. The consulate is running out of funds and allows them to be broken. It is already a feeling of the past and the present. Unfortunately, it was suddenly destroyed. Thinking of the chaotic state, I don't know what the readers will think.

The Korean people's views on China can be roughly divided into four factions. The elderly people over fifty years old are still kind. They recall that during the eighth year of Guangxu, Li Hongzhang, Wu Changqing, and other former sages led troops across the sea to quell the Korean internal rebellion. They also remember the merits of Admiral Wu Zhaoyou's two suppressions of the internal rebellion. They also constantly remember China's past assistance to Korea and hope that after China becomes strong as soon as possible, it can help their weak nation again. Most ambitious young people are unwilling to succumb to the violent oppression of Japanese imperialism and come to China to participate in the revolution or study academics. They hold a "never share the same sky" determination against Japan and especially hope that our country's revolution will succeed as soon as possible. There are also a small number of young people in the country who have received sufficient education. Although they feel the pain of national subjugation, they are not free and can only resentfully pass the years. However, those factions are in the minority. The largest number of young people have been anesthetized by slavery education since childhood. They do not know what kind of nation they are or the past history of Korea and have almost assimilated into the Japanese. That group of young people is fundamentally hopeless. The crowd in this riot is also this generation of pitiable enslaved people. Now, we can only hope that the kind elderly and the revolutionary Korean youth will rise up and awaken that group of ignorant fools.

Ziliang ignored her and continued to do his own thing. The wife had no other choice, so she went downstairs. As soon as she got downstairs, she immediately came back up, holding a fast letter from Nanjing:

"When did this arrive? Why didn't you tell me?"

"It came when you were watching the grand funeral procession with such fascination. After you came back, you were so eager to admire the playboy's sister-in-law that I didn't have time to tell you."

"What's the matter? Who's letter is this?"

"Don't you know? This is a letter from my good friend, Ye Yunyu. She's coming to Shanghai from Nanjing today. She should arrive at our house at 2:30. Let's go change our clothes."

"Why should I change my clothes just because she's coming?"

At this time, Ziliang thought of Ye Yunyu and became worried, because Ye Yunyu was another troublemaker. She was very small, but her voice was very loud. Last year, her husband got a job at the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, so she moved her family there. Ziliang's house has not seen Cicada since. She is Yueru's good friend. The two of them together, how can anything get done today?

"You're so embarrassing! Yunyu's husband has become an official. You've been messing around for years and are still just a schoolteacher. Aren't you ashamed? If you go out to meet a guest in an old cotton gown, my face will be completely ruined."

"Officials are certainly respectable, and playboys are also wealthy. In your eyes, only schoolteachers are poor?"

Yueru ignored him and rushed to the front room. At the same time, she called the nanny to come upstairs to help her open the suitcase, find clothes, wash her face, and apply powder, which greatly affected the small attic. After a while, the nanny went downstairs. Presumably, she had finished her makeup. The sound of high-heeled shoes suddenly appeared in the small attic, and a neatly dressed lady appeared.

Flour Market Plunges in the Afternoon 286

Rumors Abound of a Certain Factory Releasing a Large Batch

Yesterday, in the flour market, after the opening of the market in the morning, the prices of each month were still stable, because the quotation of foreign wheat, although it continued to fall by 2-3 jiao, and the weather had turned clear, the situation of rising due to rain must still be tired. However, the mainland bulls always held firm and did not want to return, and the factory's sale of goods was also sporadic, so the opening price of each month was not much different from the previous day. Until the afternoon market opened, the situation of each month suddenly became depressed. The sharpness of the decline was similar to the rising wind of the previous day, because the price of foreign flour was only called 2 yuan 6 jiao, and it was rumored that a certain large factory would release a large batch, and general speculators seemed to strike first and make a major return, and the market gradually plunged sharply. Speaking frankly, according to the water situation in the mainland, looking at the bigger picture is still reasonable, but looking back on foreign countries, the quotation of foreign wheat has been low for 5-6 days in a row, and it is still not free from surplus, so it is difficult for people's hearts in the country to resist the comparison of foreign prices. As a result, this month fell by 2 fen from the previous day, August fell by 2 fen 2 li half, September fell by 2 fen, October fell by 1 fen 7 li half, November fell by 2 fen, and December fell by 1 fen half, it was said.

Futures Wheat Plunges by 7-8 Fen 287

Yesterday, after the opening of the futures wheat market in the morning, the market of each month had already shown signs of fatigue, because the quotation of foreign wheat was again low by 2-3 jiao, and most people could not help but be suspicious because of this, but there were still few sellers and the degree of decline was also slight. Until the afternoon market opened, the near and far periods were again hit hard, because the foreign firms' foreign wheat price was only called 4 taels 3 qian 6 fen, and if they wanted to set a price, they would listen to the Chinese merchants' bids, which greatly stimulated people's hearts, and the selling sentiment suddenly increased, and the market plunged sharply, falling by 6, 7, or 8 fen. Looking at the future trend, with the open road of foreign wheat, simply picking up hard seems inappropriate. As a result, this month fell by 6 fen from the previous day, August, September, and October fell by 7 fen, November fell by 8 fen, and December fell by 4 fen. The current wheat market situation is still average, because the big factories have not moved, and the bottom is gradually thickening. In recent days, only small and medium-sized factories have had slight exchanges, opening 2600+ bags of Taicang, Taizhou, Benniu, Nanjing, Yangzhou, Xuzhou, Penglai, Shuangfeng, and Hezhou wheat, which were handled by Xiangxin and Xinda.

Wuxi Summer Silkworms Damaged by Rainwater 289

In Wuxi's various markets and villages, this year's summer silkworm feeding was quite smooth, but the feeding was uneven, with both foreign and local breeds being bred. After receiving the ants, the weather was sunny and warm, and the development was smooth, but after the third sleep, there were continuous rainfalls, coupled with sultry heat and sudden cold. The early silkworms in the middle of the big sleep were found to have diseases such as diarrhea and black vomit due to eating rainwater leaves. The late silkworms with sufficient leaves in the third sleep were all lying stiff and unable to sleep, and most of them were stiffly dead. Mulberry leaves had a line but no market. The harvest of this year's Wuxi summer silkworms must still be poor, and the silkworm farmers were all frowning, and the loss of silkworm books was considerable.

Shanghai Market

Market News 313

The Lihua Company on Nanjing Road declares: Our company has recently received new batches of Grand Band Gramophone records, Series Six of the Gramophone Company and Series Eleven of the Pathé record, with numerous titles and beautiful music. They are most suitable for adjusting a tedious life. The performers are famous actors and great musicians, so music lovers have been rushing to buy them.

The Sifang Company at 68 Avenue Edward VII declares: Our company pioneered the handkerchief washing department, and its business is exceptionally thriving. The laundry department was reorganized some time ago and suspended collection and delivery. We have now strived for improvements and are generally ready. We have also selected the tenth of this month for the official reopening. We have hired outstanding technicians to use mechanized chemical methods to meticulously wash Chinese and Western clothes. We have also added an express clothing department where items can be picked up on the same day. For the convenience of customers, we have switched to using value coupons, each worth five cents, and every twenty-one coupons are sold for only one dollar to show preferential treatment.

Publishing News 314

Typing is a skill necessary for businesses. However, without suitable textbooks, students have nowhere to turn. Typing instructor Xu Changqing, in view of this, based on his experience in the YMCA typing course, has compiled the book "Typing Speed Method." The content includes mechanical operation methods, nomenclature, fingering methods, and practice curriculum methods. It is very complete. If students purchase this book and follow the rules and regulations in the book, and practice for one hour each day, they will be able to type fifty words per minute with their eyes closed in one day. In order to promote this widely, each book is priced at only 60 cents. The book is sold at the Educational Department of the YMCA on Sichuan Road, the Dahua Magazine Company on Sichuan Road, the Commercial Press on Henan Road, and the Youth Association Bookstore at 20 Museum Road.

The Bailian Literary Society at 2 Yuanyuan Lane, Tientong'an Road, declares: Our society publishes a semi-monthly journal of youth literature. The content is entirely devoted to publishing outstanding youth works and discussing literary and artistic subjects. The inaugural issue has now been published. The consignment point is located at 126 South of the Grand French Avenue on the East Zilaihuo Street. Each copy sells for three copper coins.

Medical News 315

Physician Chen Peichun declares: I am proficient in Western medicine and have many years of clinical experience. In order to facilitate the treatment of patients and provide charitable assistance, I have specially opened the Tiande Hospital in the middle of Laojie Road. I have also invited the national doctor, Mr. Ni Jiaochu, to assist in the treatment of internal medicine. The arrangements are perfect, and we specialize in charity to benefit patients. Medical and drug fees are not charged; only a registration fee of ten copper coins is charged.
